This event prompted the <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Center" title="Simon Wiesenthal Center">Simon Wiesenthal Center</a> to publicly issue a protest to the Croatian president.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Cases of displaying Ustashe memorabilia have been recorded at the commemoration for the <a href="/wiki/Bleiburg_repatriations" title="Bleiburg repatriations">Bleiburg repatriations</a> held annually in <a href="/wiki/Bleiburg" title="Bleiburg">Bleiburg</a>, Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An example of neo-Nazism in Serbia is the group <a href="/wiki/Nacionalni_stroj" class="mw-redirect" title="Nacionalni stroj">Nacionalni stroj</a>. In 2006 charges were brought against 18 leading members.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The other organization was <a href="/wiki/Obraz_(organization)" title="Obraz (organization)">Obraz</a> which was banned on 12 June 2012 by <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Serbia" title="Constitutional Court of Serbia">Constitutional Court of Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Besides political parties, there are a few militant neo-nazi organizations in Serbia, such as <a href="/wiki/Blood_%26_Honour" title="Blood &amp; Honour">Blood &amp; Honour Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Combat_18" title="Combat 18">Combat 18</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Becs%C3%BClet_napja_1997-02-15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Becs%C3%BClet_napja_1997-02-15.jpg/220px-Becs%C3%BClet_napja_1997-02-15.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Becs%C3%BClet_napja_1997-02-15.jpg/330px-Becs%C3%BClet_napja_1997-02-15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Becs%C3%BClet_napja_1997-02-15.jpg/440px-Becs%C3%BClet_napja_1997-02-15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="778" data-file-height="606" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Becs%C3%BClet_napja_1997-02-15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Hungaria Skins" with a flag evoking the Arrow Cross in 1997.</div></div></div>
<p>In Hungary, the historical political party which allied itself ideologically with German National Socialism and drew inspiration from it, was the <a href="/wiki/Arrow_Cross_Party" title="Arrow Cross Party">Arrow Cross Party</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ferenc_Sz%C3%A1lasi" title="Ferenc Szálasi">Ferenc Szálasi</a>. They referred to themselves explicitly as National Socialists and within Hungarian politics this tendency is known as <a href="/wiki/Hungarism" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarism">Hungarism</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> After the Second World War, exiles such as <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rp%C3%A1d_Henney" title="Árpád Henney">Árpád Henney</a> kept the Hungarist tradition alive. Following the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic" title="Hungarian People&#39;s Republic">Hungarian People's Republic</a> in 1989, which was a <a href="/wiki/Marxist-Leninist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist-Leninist">Marxist-Leninist</a> state and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>, many new parties emerged. Amongst these was the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_National_Front" title="Hungarian National Front">Hungarian National Front</a> of <a href="/wiki/Istv%C3%A1n_Gy%C5%91rk%C3%B6s" title="István Győrkös">István Győrkös</a>, which was a Hungarist party and considered itself the heirs of Arrow Cross-style National Socialism (a self-description they explicitly embraced);<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> it forged links with <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_K%C3%BCssel" title="Gottfried Küssel">Gottfried Küssel</a> and the NSDAP/AO.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In the 2000s, Győrkös' movement moved closer to a <a href="/wiki/National_communist" class="mw-redirect" title="National communist">national communist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neo-Eurasian" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Eurasian">neo-Eurasian</a> position, aligned with <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Dugin" title="Aleksandr Dugin">Aleksandr Dugin</a>, cooperating with the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Workers%27_Party" title="Hungarian Workers&#39; Party">Hungarian Workers' Party</a>. Some Hungarists opposed this and founded the <a href="/wiki/Pax_Hungarica_Movement" title="Pax Hungarica Movement">Pax Hungarica Movement</a>. 
</p><p>In modern Hungary, the ultranationalist <a href="/wiki/Jobbik" title="Jobbik">Jobbik</a> is regarded by some scholars as a neo-Nazi party; for example, it has been termed as such by <a href="/wiki/Randolph_L._Braham" title="Randolph L. Braham">Randolph L. Braham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The party denies being neo-Nazi, although "there is extensive proof that the leading members of the party made no effort to hide their racism and anti-Semitism."<sup id="cite_ref-Spectrum_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spectrum-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Rudolf Paksa, a scholar of the Hungarian far right, describes Jobbik as "anti-Semitic, racist, homophobic and chauvinistic" but not as neo-Nazi because it does not pursue the establishment of a totalitarian regime.<sup id="cite_ref-Spectrum_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spectrum-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Kriszti%C3%A1n_Ungv%C3%A1ry" title="Krisztián Ungváry">Krisztián Ungváry</a> writes that "It is safe to say that certain messages of Jobbik can be called open neo-Nazi propaganda. However, it is quite certain that the popularity of the party is not due to these statements."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Romania, the ultra-nationalist movement which allied itself with the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> and German National Socialism was the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Guard" title="Iron Guard">Iron Guard</a>, also known as the Legion of the Archangel Michael. There are some modern political organisations which consider themselves heirs of Legionarism, this includes <a href="/wiki/Noua_Dreapt%C4%83" title="Noua Dreaptă">Noua Dreaptă</a> and the <a href="/wiki/%22Everything_For_the_Country%22_Party" title="&quot;Everything For the Country&quot; Party">"Everything For the Country" Party</a>, founded by former Iron Guard members. The latter organisation was outlawed in 2015. Aside, from these Romanian organisations, the <a href="/wiki/Sixty-Four_Counties_Youth_Movement" title="Sixty-Four Counties Youth Movement">Sixty-Four Counties Youth Movement</a> representing ultra-nationalism from the Hungarian minority is also present, especially in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Other nationalistic and irridentist groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Romania_Party" title="Greater Romania Party">Greater Romania Party</a> do not originate from Legionarism, but in fact grew out of <a href="/wiki/National_communist" class="mw-redirect" title="National communist">national communist</a> tendencies from the era of <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C8%99escu" title="Nicolae Ceaușescu">Nicolae Ceaușescu</a> (the party was founded by his "court poet" <a href="/wiki/Corneliu_Vadim_Tudor" title="Corneliu Vadim Tudor">Corneliu Vadim Tudor</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PU-Kyiv.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/PU-Kyiv.jpg/220px-PU-Kyiv.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/PU-Kyiv.jpg/330px-PU-Kyiv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/PU-Kyiv.jpg/440px-PU-Kyiv.jpg 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="474" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PU-Kyiv.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protesters with neo-Nazi symbols – <a href="/wiki/14th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(1st_Galician)" title="14th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Galician)">SS-Volunteer Division "Galicia"</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patriot_of_Ukraine" title="Patriot of Ukraine">Patriot of Ukraine</a> flags</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2014-07-24._%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%96%D1%87_004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/2014-07-24._%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%96%D1%87_004.jpg/220px-2014-07-24._%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%96%D1%87_004.jpg" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/2014-07-24._%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%96%D1%87_004.jpg/330px-2014-07-24._%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%96%D1%87_004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/2014-07-24._%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%96%D1%87_004.jpg/440px-2014-07-24._%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%96%D1%87_004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1673" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2014-07-24._%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B9%D0%BE%D0%BD_%D0%A1%D1%96%D1%87_004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_volunteer_battalions_(since_2014)" title="Ukrainian volunteer battalions (since 2014)">Ukrainian volunteer battalion</a> members with neo-Nazi <i><a href="/wiki/Wolfsangel" title="Wolfsangel">Wolfsangel</a></i> symbol, 24 July 2014</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Racism_and_discrimination_in_Ukraine" title="Racism and discrimination in Ukraine">Racism and discrimination in Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_nationalism" title="Ukrainian nationalism">Ukrainian nationalism</a></div>
<p>In 1991 <a href="/wiki/Svoboda_(political_party)" title="Svoboda (political party)">Svoboda</a> was founded as the <a href="/wiki/Social-National_Party_of_Ukraine" title="Social-National Party of Ukraine">Social-National Party of Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The party combined <a href="/wiki/Radical_nationalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Radical nationalism">radical nationalism</a> and neo-Nazi features.<sup id="cite_ref-konotop_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-konotop-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ibtimes_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> It was renamed and rebranded 13 years later as All-Ukrainian Association Svoboda in 2004 under <a href="/wiki/Oleh_Tyahnybok" title="Oleh Tyahnybok">Oleh Tyahnybok</a>. In 2016, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Nation" title="The Nation">The Nation</a></i> reported that "in Ukrainian municipal elections held [in October 2015], the neo-Nazi Svoboda party won 10 percent of the vote in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> and placed second in <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">Lviv</a>. The Svoboda party’s candidate actually won the mayoral election in the city of <a href="/wiki/Konotop" title="Konotop">Konotop</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-nation_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nation-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The Svoboda party mayor in Konotop reportedly has the number "<a href="/wiki/14/88" class="mw-redirect" title="14/88">14/88</a>" displayed on his car and has refused to display the city's official flag because it contains a <a href="/wiki/Star_of_David" title="Star of David">star of David</a>, and has implied that Jews were responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">Holodomor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-konotop_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-konotop-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The topic of Ukrainian nationalism and its alleged relationship to neo-Nazism came to the fore in polemics about the more radical elements involved in the <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a> protests and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_crisis" title="Ukrainian crisis">Ukrainian crisis</a> from 2013 onward.<sup id="cite_ref-ibtimes_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Some Russian, Latin American, U.S. and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> media have attempted to portray the Ukrainian nationalists in the conflict as neo-Nazi.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The main Ukrainian organisations involved with a neo-Banderaite legacy are <a href="/wiki/Right_Sector" title="Right Sector">Right Sector</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Svoboda_(political_party)" title="Svoboda (political party)">Svoboda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azov_Battalion" title="Azov Battalion">Azov Battalion</a>. The persons regarded as Ukraine's national heroes — <a href="/wiki/Stepan_Bandera" title="Stepan Bandera">Stepan Bandera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Shukhevych" title="Roman Shukhevych">Roman Shukhevych</a> or <a href="/wiki/Dmytro_Klyachkivsky" title="Dmytro Klyachkivsky">Dmytro Klyachkivsky</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ukrainian_Nationalists" title="Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists">Organization of Ukrainian Nationalists</a> (OUN) and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army" title="Ukrainian Insurgent Army">Ukrainian Insurgent Army</a> (UPA) — at times supported and then opposed the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a> in Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Yanokovych's ouster in February 2014, the interim <a href="/wiki/First_Yatsenyuk_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="First Yatsenyuk Government">Yatsenyuk Government</a> placed 4 Svoboda members in leading positions: <a href="/wiki/Oleksandr_Sych" title="Oleksandr Sych">Oleksandr Sych</a> as Vice Prime Minister of Ukraine, <a href="/wiki/Ihor_Tenyukh" title="Ihor Tenyukh">Ihor Tenyukh</a> as Minister of Defense, lawyer <a href="/wiki/Ihor_Shvaika" title="Ihor Shvaika">Ihor Shvaika</a> as Minister of Agrarian Policy and Food and <a href="/wiki/Andriy_Mokhnyk" title="Andriy Mokhnyk">Andriy Mokhnyk</a> as Minister of Ecology and Natural Resources of Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-channel14_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-channel14-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Since 14 April 2016 the <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Ukrainian_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman of the Ukrainian Parliament">Chairman of the Ukrainian Parliament</a> has been <a href="/wiki/Andriy_Parubiy" title="Andriy Parubiy">Andriy Parubiy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> the co-founder of the neo-Nazi Social-National Party of Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-channel14_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-channel14-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2015, Democratic Representative <a href="/wiki/John_Conyers" title="John Conyers">John Conyers</a> and his Republican colleague <a href="/wiki/Ted_Yoho" title="Ted Yoho">Ted Yoho</a> offered bipartisan amendments to block the U.S. military training of Ukraine's <a href="/wiki/Azov_Battalion" title="Azov Battalion">Azov Battalion</a> — called a “neo-Nazi paramilitary militia” by Conyers and Yoho.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nation_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nation-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andriy_Biletsky_(politician)" title="Andriy Biletsky (politician)">Andriy Biletsky</a>, the head of the ultra-nationalist and neo-Nazi political groups <a href="/wiki/Social-National_Assembly" title="Social-National Assembly">Social-National Assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patriots_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Patriots of Ukraine">Patriots of Ukraine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> has been commander of the Azov Battalion.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Azov Battalion of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_National_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian National Guard">Ukrainian National Guard</a><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> is fighting pro-Russian separatists in the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbass" title="War in Donbass">War in Donbass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Some members of the battalion are openly <a href="/wiki/White_supremacy" title="White supremacy">white supremacists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Issues">Issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ex-Nazis_in_mainstream_politics">Ex-Nazis in mainstream politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ex-Nazis in mainstream politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kurt_Waldheim_1971b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Kurt_Waldheim_1971b.jpg/220px-Kurt_Waldheim_1971b.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Kurt_Waldheim_1971b.jpg/330px-Kurt_Waldheim_1971b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Kurt_Waldheim_1971b.jpg/440px-Kurt_Waldheim_1971b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="813" data-file-height="1084" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kurt_Waldheim_1971b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1980s dispute between Austrian president <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Waldheim" title="Kurt Waldheim">Kurt Waldheim</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Jewish_Congress" title="World Jewish Congress">World Jewish Congress</a> caused an international incident.</div></div></div>
<p>The most significant case on an international level was the election of <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Waldheim" title="Kurt Waldheim">Kurt Waldheim</a> to the Presidency of Austria in 1986. It came to light that Waldheim had been a member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_German_Students%27_League" title="National Socialist German Students&#39; League">National Socialist German Students' League</a>, the SA and served as an intelligence officer during the Second World War. Following this he served as an Austrian diplomat and was the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a> from 1972 until 1981. After revelations of Waldheim's past were made by an Austrian journalist, Waldheim clashed with the <a href="/wiki/World_Jewish_Congress" title="World Jewish Congress">World Jewish Congress</a> on the international stage. Waldheim's record was defended by <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Kreisky" title="Bruno Kreisky">Bruno Kreisky</a>, an Austrian Jew who served as Chancellor of Austria. The legacy of the affair lingers on, as <a href="/wiki/Victor_Ostrovsky" title="Victor Ostrovsky">Victor Ostrovsky</a> has claimed the <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a> doctored the file of Waldheim to implicate him in war crimes.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_right-wing_populism">Contemporary right-wing populism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Contemporary right-wing populism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some critics have sought to draw a connection between Nazism and modern <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_populism" title="Right-wing populism">right-wing populism</a> in Europe, but the two are not widely regarded as interchangeable by most academics. In Austria, the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Party_of_Austria" title="Freedom Party of Austria">Freedom Party of Austria</a> (FPÖ) served as a shelter for ex-Nazis almost from its inception.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1980, scandals undermined Austria's two main parties and the economy stagnated. <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B6rg_Haider" title="Jörg Haider">Jörg Haider</a> became leader of the FPÖ and offered partial justification for <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a>, calling its employment policy effective. In the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_legislative_election,_1994" title="Austrian legislative election, 1994">1994 Austrian election</a>, the FPÖ won 22 percent of the vote, as well as 33 percent of the vote in <a href="/wiki/Carinthia_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Carinthia (state)">Carinthia</a> and 22 percent in Vienna; showing that it had become a force capable of reversing the old pattern of Austrian politics.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historian <a href="/wiki/Walter_Laqueur" title="Walter Laqueur">Walter Laqueur</a> writes that even though Haider welcomed former Nazis at his meetings and went out of his way to address <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">Schutzstaffel</a> (SS) veterans, the FPÖ is not a fascist party in the traditional sense, since it has not made <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communism</a> an important issue, and it does not advocate the overthrow of the democratic order or the use of violence. In his view, the FPÖ is "not quite fascist", although it is part of a tradition, similar to that of 19th-century Viennese mayor <a href="/wiki/Karl_Lueger" title="Karl Lueger">Karl Lueger</a>, which involves <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>, xenophobic populism, and <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarianism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Haider, who in 2005 left the Freedom Party and formed the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Austria%27s_Future" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance for Austria&#39;s Future">Alliance for Austria's Future</a>, was killed in a traffic accident in October 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Barbara_Rosenkranz" title="Barbara Rosenkranz">Barbara Rosenkranz</a>, the Freedom Party's candidate for the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_presidential_election,_2010" title="Austrian presidential election, 2010">Austrian presidential election, 2010</a>, is controversial for having made allegedly pro-Nazi statements.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Rosenkranz is married to <a href="/wiki/Horst_Rosenkranz" title="Horst Rosenkranz">Horst Rosenkranz</a>, a key member of a banned neo-Nazi party, who is known for publishing far-right books. Rosenkranz says she cannot detect anything "dishonourable" in her husband's activities.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Around_the_world">Around the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Around the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Batallon_de_Castigo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Batallon_de_Castigo.jpg/250px-Batallon_de_Castigo.jpg" width="250" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Batallon_de_Castigo.jpg/375px-Batallon_de_Castigo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d2/Batallon_de_Castigo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="442" data-file-height="291" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Batallon_de_Castigo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Neo-Nazi skinheads in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a></div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Belgium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bloed,_Bodem,_Eer_en_Trouw" title="Bloed, Bodem, Eer en Trouw">Bloed, Bodem, Eer en Trouw</a></div>
<p>A Belgian neo-Nazi organization, <a href="/wiki/Bloed,_Bodem,_Eer_en_Trouw" title="Bloed, Bodem, Eer en Trouw">Bloed, Bodem, Eer en Trouw</a> (Blood, Soil, Honour and Loyalty), was created in 2004 after splitting from the international network (<a href="/wiki/Blood_and_Honour" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood and Honour">Blood and Honour</a>). The group rose to public prominence in September 2006, after 17 members (including 11 soldiers) were arrested under the December 2003 <a href="/wiki/Anti-terrorism_legislation" title="Anti-terrorism legislation">anti-terrorist laws</a> and laws against <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitism</a> and supporters of <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a>. According to Justice Minister <a href="/wiki/Laurette_Onkelinx" title="Laurette Onkelinx">Laurette Onkelinx</a> and Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Dewael" title="Patrick Dewael">Patrick Dewael</a>, the suspects (11 of whom were members of the military) were preparing to launch terrorist attacks in order to "destabilize" <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> According to the journalist Manuel Abramowicz, of the Resistances,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> the extremists  of the radical right have always had as its aim to "infiltrate the state mechanisms," including the army in the 1970s and the 1980s, through <a href="/wiki/Westland_New_Post" title="Westland New Post">Westland New Post</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Front_de_la_Jeunesse_(Belgium)" title="Front de la Jeunesse (Belgium)">Front de la Jeunesse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A police operation, which mobilized 150 agents, searched five military barracks (in <a href="/wiki/Leopoldsburg" title="Leopoldsburg">Leopoldsburg</a> near the Dutch border, Kleine-Brogel, <a href="/wiki/Peer,_Belgium" title="Peer, Belgium">Peer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> (Royal military school) and <a href="/wiki/Zedelgem" title="Zedelgem">Zedelgem</a>) as well as 18 private addresses in <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>. They found weapons, munitions, explosives and a homemade bomb large enough to make "a car explode". The leading suspect, B.T., was organizing the trafficking of weapons and was developing international links, in particular with the Dutch far-right movement <a href="/wiki/National_Alliance_(Netherlands)" title="National Alliance (Netherlands)">De Nationale Alliantie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bosnia and Herzegovina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The neo-Nazi <a href="/wiki/White_nationalism" title="White nationalism">white nationalist</a> organization Bosanski Pokret Nacionalnog Ponosa (<a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Movement_of_National_Pride" title="Bosnian Movement of National Pride">Bosnian Movement of National Pride</a>) was founded in <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> in July 2009. Its model is the <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS" title="Waffen-SS">Waffen-SS</a> <a href="/wiki/13th_Waffen_Mountain_Division_of_the_SS_Handschar_(1st_Croatian)" title="13th Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Handschar (1st Croatian)">Handschar Division</a>, which was composed of <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniak</a> volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> It proclaimed its main enemies to be "<a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a>, Serbian <a href="/wiki/Chetniks" title="Chetniks">Chetniks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Croatian_Republic_of_Herzeg-Bosnia" title="Croatian Republic of Herzeg-Bosnia">Croatian separatists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">blacks</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Its ideology is a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_nationalism" title="Bosnian nationalism">Bosnian nationalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">National Socialism</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_nationalism" title="White nationalism">white nationalism</a>. It says ""Ideologies that are not welcome in Bosnia are: Zionism, Islamism, communism, capitalism. The only ideology good for us is Bosnian nationalism because it secures national prosperity and social justice..."<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The group is led by a person nicknamed Sauberzwig, after the commander of the 13th SS Handschar. The group's strongest area of operations is in the Tuzla area of Bosnia.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic">Czech Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Czech Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The government of the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> strictly punishes neo-Nazism (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i>Neonacismus</i>). According to a report by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Interior_of_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of the Interior of the Czech Republic">Ministry of the Interior of the Czech Republic</a>, neo-Nazis committed more than 211 crimes in 2013. The Czech Republic has more than 150 members of various neo-Nazi groups. One of them is the group Wotan Jugend, based in Germany.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Estonia">Estonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Estonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2006, Roman Ilin, a Jewish theatre director from <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, was attacked by neo-Nazis when returning from an underground tunnel after a rehearsal. Ilin subsequently accused Estonian police of indifference after filing the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> When a dark-skinned <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> student was attacked in <a href="/wiki/Tartu" title="Tartu">Tartu</a>, the head of an association of foreign students claimed that the attack was characteristic of a wave of neo-Nazi violence. An Estonian police official, however, stated that there were only a few cases involving foreign students over the previous two years.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In November 2006, the Estonian government passed a law banning the display of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_symbolism" title="Nazi symbolism">Nazi symbols</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2008 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> Special Rapporteur's Report noted that community representatives and non-governmental organizations devoted to human rights had pointed out that neo-Nazi groups were active in Estonia—particularly in Tartu—and had perpetrated acts of violence against non-European minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Far-right_politics_in_Germany" title="Far-right politics in Germany">Far-right politics in Germany</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationale_sozialisten_leipzig_recht_auf_zukunft.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nationale_sozialisten_leipzig_recht_auf_zukunft.jpg/220px-Nationale_sozialisten_leipzig_recht_auf_zukunft.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nationale_sozialisten_leipzig_recht_auf_zukunft.jpg/330px-Nationale_sozialisten_leipzig_recht_auf_zukunft.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nationale_sozialisten_leipzig_recht_auf_zukunft.jpg/440px-Nationale_sozialisten_leipzig_recht_auf_zukunft.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationale_sozialisten_leipzig_recht_auf_zukunft.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Neo-Nazi demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>, Germany in October 2009</div></div></div>
<p>According to the annual report of Germany's interior intelligence service (Verfassungsschutz) for 2012, at the time there were 26,000 right-wing extremists living in Germany, including 6,000 neo-Nazis.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The neo-Nazi organizations are not outlawed in Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> although <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_denial" title="Holocaust denial">Holocaust denial</a> is a crime, according to the German Criminal Code (<a href="/wiki/Strafgesetzbuch_%C2%A7_86a" class="mw-redirect" title="Strafgesetzbuch § 86a">Strafgesetzbuch § 86a</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Laws_against_Holocaust_denial#Germany" title="Laws against Holocaust denial">§ 130 (public incitement)</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Meandros_flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Meandros_flag.svg/220px-Meandros_flag.svg.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Meandros_flag.svg/330px-Meandros_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Meandros_flag.svg/440px-Meandros_flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="405" data-file-height="270" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Meandros_flag.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Dawn_(Greece)" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Dawn (Greece)">Golden Dawn</a></div></div></div>
<p>In April 1967, a few weeks prior to an election, a military coup d'état took place in Greece and a fascist military government ruled the country from 1967 to 1974. It was called the "<a href="/wiki/Greek_military_junta_of_1967%E2%80%9374" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek military junta of 1967–74">Regime of the Colonels</a>", and was headed by Colonel <a href="/wiki/Georgios_Papadopoulos" title="Georgios Papadopoulos">Georgios Papadopoulos</a>. The official reason given for the coup was that a "communist conspiracy" had infiltrated all levels of society.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although there have been persistent rumors about an active support of the coup by the U.S. government, there is no evidence to support such claims.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>  The timing of the coup apparently caught the CIA by surprise.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The contemporary Greek political party <a href="/wiki/Golden_Dawn_(Greece)" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Dawn (Greece)">Golden Dawn</a> (Χρυσή Αυγή - Chrysi Avyi), which found its roots in Papadopoulos' regime, has been described as subscribing to neo-fascist and neo-Nazi beliefs and practices.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The far right political is generally labelled neo-Nazi, although the group rejects this label. A few Golden Dawn members participated in the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Volunteer_Guard" title="Greek Volunteer Guard">Greek Volunteer Guard</a> (GVG) and were present in <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica" title="Srebrenica">Srebrenica</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica_massacre#Non-Serb_participants_in_the_killings" title="Srebrenica massacre">Srebrenica massacre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Michas_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michas-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-srebr_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-srebr-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Golden Dawn has spoken out in favour of the Assad regime in Syria,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and the Strasserist group Black Lily have claimed to have sent mercenaries to Syria to fight alongside the Syrian regime, specifically mentioning their participation in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_al-Qusayr_(2013)" title="Battle of al-Qusayr (2013)">Battle of al-Qusayr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the elections of 6 May 2012, Golden Dawn received 6.97% of the votes, entering the Greek parliament for the first time with 21 representatives. Due to no coalition amongst the elected parties so as to form a Greek Government, new elections were proclaimed.
</p><p>In the elections of 17 June 2012, Golden Dawn received 6.92% of the votes, entering the Greek parliament with 18 representatives.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Coordination Forum for Countering Antisemitism reports that on 17 May 2011 in <a href="/wiki/Leek,_Netherlands" title="Leek, Netherlands">Leek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Groningen_(province)" title="Groningen (province)">Groningen</a>, antisemitic graffiti was found at a Jewish school. The graffiti consisted of a swastika and the text "C18", or <a href="/wiki/Combat_18" title="Combat 18">Combat 18</a>, a neo-Nazi organisation active throughout Europe. The number 18 refers to the initials of Adolf Hitler, A and H being the first and eighth letters of the alphabet, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ONR_poznan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/ONR_poznan.jpg/250px-ONR_poznan.jpg" width="250" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/ONR_poznan.jpg/375px-ONR_poznan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/ONR_poznan.jpg/500px-ONR_poznan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ONR_poznan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ONR march in <a href="/wiki/Pozna%C5%84" title="Poznań">Poznań</a> in November 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Constitution">Polish Constitution</a> promoting any totalitarian system such as <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascism</a> (as well as <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a>) as well as inciting violence and/or racial hatred is illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> This was further re-enforced in the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Penal_Code" title="Polish Penal Code">Polish Penal Code</a> where discrediting any group or persons on national, religious, racial or religious grounds carries a sentence of 3 years.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although several small far-right and anti-semitic organisations exist, most notably <a href="/wiki/National_Revival_of_Poland" title="National Revival of Poland">NOP</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Radical_Camp_(1993)" title="National Radical Camp (1993)">ONR</a> (both of which exist legally), they frequently adhere to <a href="/wiki/Polish_nationalism" title="Polish nationalism">Polish nationalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Democracy" title="National Democracy">National Democracy</a>, in which Nazism is generally considered to be against <a href="/wiki/Ultra-nationalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultra-nationalism">ultra-nationalist</a> principles, and although they are classed as <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> movements, they are at the same time considered anti-Nazi. Some of their elements may resemble neo-Nazi features, but these groups frequently dissociate themselves from Nazi elements, claiming that such acts are unpatriotic and they argue that Nazism misappropriated or slightly altered several pre-existing symbols and features, such as distinguishing the <a href="/wiki/Roman_salute" title="Roman salute">Roman salute</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_salute" title="Nazi salute">Nazi salute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dziennik.pl(2008-06-21)_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dziennik.pl(2008-06-21)-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Self-declared neo-nazi movements in Poland frequently treat Polish culture and traditions with contempt, are <a href="/wiki/Anti-Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Christian">anti-Christian</a> and translate various texts from German, meaning they are considered movements favouring <a href="/wiki/Germanisation" title="Germanisation">Germanisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>.
</p><p>According to several reporter investigations the Polish government turns a blind eye to these groups and they are free to spread their ideology, frequently dismissing their existence as <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theories" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy theories">conspiracy theories</a>, dismissing acts political provocations, deeming them too insignificant to pose a threat, or <a href="/wiki/Apologetics" title="Apologetics">attempting to justify or diminish the seriousness of their actions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_Russia" title="Racism in Russia">Racism in Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radical_nationalism_in_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Radical nationalism in Russia">Radical nationalism in Russia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neo-Nazism_in_Russia_(2010).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Neo-Nazism_in_Russia_%282010%29.jpg/170px-Neo-Nazism_in_Russia_%282010%29.jpg" width="170" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Neo-Nazism_in_Russia_%282010%29.jpg/255px-Neo-Nazism_in_Russia_%282010%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Neo-Nazism_in_Russia_%282010%29.jpg/340px-Neo-Nazism_in_Russia_%282010%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="384" data-file-height="556" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Neo-Nazism_in_Russia_(2010).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Neo-Nazism in Russia: The photograph was taken at an anti-gay demonstration in Moscow in October 2010</div></div></div>
<p>There are a few Russian neo-Nazis that openly admire <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> and use the <a href="/wiki/Swastika" title="Swastika">swastika</a> as their symbol. Russian neo-Nazis are characterized by <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">homophobia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islamophobia" title="Islamophobia">Islamophobia</a> and extreme <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">xenophobia</a> towards people from <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Their ideology centers on defending Russian national identity against what they perceive as a takeover by minority groups such as <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Caucasus" title="Peoples of the Caucasus">Caucasians</a>, gay people, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asians</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma people</a> (gypsies), and Muslims. There is also a widespread gay rights Nazi skinhead subculture with its own Vkontakte group, GASH, and an alleged 1700 members in Moscow alone.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Russian neo-Nazis have made it an explicit goal to take over the country by force, and have put serious effort into preparing for this. <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">Paramilitary</a> organizations operating under the guise of sports clubs have trained their members in squad tactics, <a href="/wiki/Hand_to_hand_combat" class="mw-redirect" title="Hand to hand combat">hand to hand combat</a> and weapons handling. They have stockpiled and used weapons, often illegally.
</p><p>Some observers have noted a subjective irony of Russians embracing Nazism, because one of Hitler's ambitions at the start of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Generalplan Ost</a> (Master Plan East) which envisaged to exterminate, expel, or enslave most or all Slavs from central and eastern Europe (e.g., Russians, Ukrainians, Poles etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-William1_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-William1-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Russian neo-Nazis deny the authenticity of this plan and instead emphasize the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">1939-1941 Nazi-Soviet non-aggression pact</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-William1_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-William1-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_invasion_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi invasion of the Soviet Union">Nazi invasion of the Soviet Union</a>, over 25 million Soviet citizens had died.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In a 2007 news story, <i>ABC News</i> reported, "In a country that lost more people defeating the Nazis than any other country, there are now an estimated 50,000 to 70,000 neo-Nazis, half of the world's total."<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991 caused great economic and social problems, including widespread <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>. Several <a href="/wiki/Far_right" class="mw-redirect" title="Far right">far right</a> <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitary</a> organizations were able to tap into popular discontent, particularly among marginalized, lesser educated and unemployed youths. Of the three major age groups — youths, adults, and the elderly — youths may have been hit the hardest. The elderly suffered due to inadequate (or unpaid) pensions, but they found effective political representation in the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Communist Party of the Russian Federation">Communist Party</a>, and generally had their concerns addressed through better budget allocations. Adults, although often suffering financially and psychologically due to job losses, were generally able to find new sources of income.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Russian_National_Unity" title="Russian National Unity">Russian National Unity</a> (RNE), founded in 1990 and led by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Barkashov" title="Alexander Barkashov">Alexander Barkashov</a>, has claimed to have members in 250 cities. RNE adopted the swastika as its symbol, and sees itself as the avant-garde of a coming national revolution. It is critical of other major far right organizations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democratic_Party_of_Russia" title="Liberal Democratic Party of Russia">Liberal Democratic Party of Russia</a> (LDPR). Historian Walter Laqueur calls RNE far closer to the Nazi model than the LDPR. RNE publishes several news sheets; one of them, <i>Russky poryadok</i>, claims to have a circulation of 150,000. Full members of RNE are called Soratnik (comrades in arms), receive combat training at locations near Moscow, and many of them work as security officers or armed guards.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 August 2007, Russian authorities arrested a student for allegedly posting a video on the Internet which appears to show two migrant workers being beheaded in front of a red and black swastika flag.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Alexander Verkhovsky, the head of a Moscow-based center that monitors <a href="/wiki/Hate_crime" title="Hate crime">hate crime</a> in Russia, said, "It looks like this is the real thing. The killing is genuine ... There are similar videos from the Chechen war. But this is the first time the killing appears to have been done intentionally."<sup id="cite_ref-execution_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-execution-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Neo-Nazi activities in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> have previously been limited to <a href="/wiki/White_supremacy" title="White supremacy">white supremacist</a> groups, few of which have a membership over a few hundred members.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The main neo-Nazi organization as of 2017 is the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Resistance_Movement" title="Nordic Resistance Movement">Nordic Resistance Movement</a>. Nordic Resistance Movement self-identifies as a <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="National Socialist">National Socialist</a> political movement with a parliamentary branch. They are also active in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Far_right_in_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Far right in Switzerland">Far right in Switzerland</a></div>
<p>The neo-Nazi and <a href="/wiki/White_power_skinhead" title="White power skinhead">white power skinhead</a> scene in Switzerland has seen significant growth in the 1990s and 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> It is reflected in the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Partei_National_Orientierter_Schweizer" class="mw-redirect" title="Partei National Orientierter Schweizer">Partei National Orientierter Schweizer</a> in 2000, which resulted in an improved organizational structure of the neo-Nazi and white supremacist scene.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Turkish_nationalism" title="Turkish nationalism">Turkish nationalism</a></div>
<p>Apart from <a href="/wiki/Neo-fascist" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-fascist">neo-fascist</a><sup id="cite_ref-Political_Terrorism_p._674_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Political_Terrorism_p._674-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fascism_1993,_p._171_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fascism_1993,_p._171-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Terrorist_Groups_2003,_p._45_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Terrorist_Groups_2003,_p._45-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-consort_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-consort-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grey_Wolves_(organization)" title="Grey Wolves (organization)">Grey Wolves</a> and the Turkish <a href="/wiki/Ultranationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultranationalist">ultranationalist</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Movement_Party" title="Nationalist Movement Party">Nationalist Movement Party</a>, there are some neo-Nazi organizations in Turkey such as the Turkish Nazi Party<sup id="cite_ref-turknazipartisi_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turknazipartisi-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> or the National Socialist Party of Turkey,<sup id="cite_ref-nasyonalsosyalistturkiyepartis_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasyonalsosyalistturkiyepartis-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> which are mainly based on the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-sabah_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sabah-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hurriyet_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurriyet-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-caucasusforum.org_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caucasusforum.org-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Turkey_Party" title="National Socialist Turkey Party">National Socialist Turkey Party</a>, was founded as Turkey´s first National Socialist party.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(June 2018)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Far-right_politics_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Far-right politics in the United Kingdom">Far-right politics in the United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Racism in the United Kingdom">Racism in the United Kingdom</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_fascist_parties" title="List of British fascist parties">List of British fascist parties</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Indian subcontinent (similar to Iran) has had cultural links to the "Aryan race" and has often been a topic of discussion on race theories.
</p><p>In 1940, <a href="/wiki/Vinayak_Damodar_Savarkar" title="Vinayak Damodar Savarkar">Vinayak Damodar Savarkar</a> said, "There is no reason to suppose that Hitler must be a human monster because he passes off as a Nazi or Churchill is a demigod because he calls himself a Democrat. Nazism proved undeniably the saviour of Germany under the set of circumstances Germany was placed in. Who are we to dictate to Germany... or Italy to choose a particular form of policy of government simply?"<sup id="cite_ref-ibi_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibi-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> "Surely Hitler knows better than Pandit Nehru does what suits Germany best. The very fact that Germany or Italy has so wonderfully recovered and grown so powerful as never before at the touch of Nazi or Fascist magical wand is enough to prove that those political ‘isms’ were the most congenial tonics their health demanded."<sup id="cite_ref-ibi_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibi-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Pro-Nazi sentiment is widespread in Pakistan, according to the German magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i>, compounded by the anti-Semitism engendered by the opposition to Israel and support for Palestine general throughout the region.  Such attitudes, exemplified by a belief that Hitler was a military genius, are shared by both Muslims and Hindus, and are related to the belief that Pakistanis are Aryans, and therefore would be accepted in Nazi Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-spi_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spi-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Neo-Nazi activity is not common or widespread in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, and the few reported activities have all been the work of extremists, who were punished severely. One notable case is that of <a href="/wiki/Patrol_36" title="Patrol 36">Patrol 36</a>, a cell in <a href="/wiki/Petah_Tikva" title="Petah Tikva">Petah Tikva</a> made up of eight teenage immigrants from the former Soviet Union who had been attacking foreign workers and gay people, and vandalizing <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a> with Nazi images.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Israeli_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Israeli-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Asser_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asser-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> These neo-Nazis were reported to have operated in cities across Israel, and have been described as being influenced by the rise of neo-Nazism in Europe;<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Israeli_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Israeli-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Asser_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asser-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> mostly influenced by similar movements in Russia and Ukraine, as the rise of the phenomenon is widely credited to immigrants from those two states, the largest sources of emigration to Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Widely publicized arrests have led to a call to reform the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Return" title="Law of Return">Law of Return</a> to permit the revocation of Israeli citizenship for – and the subsequent deportation of – neo-Nazis.<sup id="cite_ref-Asser_138-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asser-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mongolia">Mongolia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Mongolia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Dayar_Mongol.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Dayar_Mongol.svg/220px-Flag_of_Dayar_Mongol.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Dayar_Mongol.svg/330px-Flag_of_Dayar_Mongol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Flag_of_Dayar_Mongol.svg/440px-Flag_of_Dayar_Mongol.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Dayar_Mongol.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the Dayar Mongol, a neo-Nazi party in Mongolia</div></div></div>
<p>From 2008, Mongolian neo-Nazi groups have defaced buildings in <a href="/wiki/Ulaanbaatar" title="Ulaanbaatar">Ulaanbaatar</a>, smashed <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a> shopkeepers' windows, and killed Chinese immigrants. The neo-Nazi Mongols' targets for violence are Chinese, <a href="/wiki/Koreans" title="Koreans">Koreans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-naive_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naive-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Mongol women who have sex with Chinese men, and <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> people.<sup id="cite_ref-mnn_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnn-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> They wear Nazi uniforms and revere the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>. Though Tsagaan Khass leaders say they do not support violence, they are self-proclaimed Nazis. "Adolf Hitler was someone we respect. He taught us how to preserve national identity," said the 41-year-old co-founder, who calls himself Big Brother. "We don't agree with his extremism and starting the Second World War. We are against all those killings, but we support his ideology. We support nationalism rather than fascism." Some have ascribed it to poor <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Mongolia" title="Education in Mongolia">historical education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-naive_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naive-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_Socialism_Association" title="National Socialism Association">National Socialism Association</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Socialism_Association" title="National Socialism Association">National Socialism Association</a> (NSA) is a neo-Nazi political organisation founded in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> in September 2006 by Hsu Na-chi (<a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hant">許娜琦</span>), at that time a 22-year-old female <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a> graduate of <a href="/wiki/Soochow_University_(Taiwan)" title="Soochow University (Taiwan)">Soochow University</a>. The NSA has an explicit stated goal of obtaining the power to govern the state. The <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Simon Wiesenthal Centre">Simon Wiesenthal Centre</a> condemned the National Socialism Association on 13 March 2007 for championing the former <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazi</a> dictator and blaming democracy for <a href="/wiki/Social_unrest" class="mw-redirect" title="Social unrest">social unrest</a> in Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz837967_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz837967-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_SUMKA.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Flag_of_SUMKA.svg/220px-Flag_of_SUMKA.svg.png" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Flag_of_SUMKA.svg/330px-Flag_of_SUMKA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Flag_of_SUMKA.svg/440px-Flag_of_SUMKA.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_SUMKA.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/SUMKA" title="SUMKA">SUMKA</a></div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/SUMKA" title="SUMKA">SUMKA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aria_Party" title="Aria Party">Aria Party</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Azure_Party" title="Azure Party">Azure Party</a></div>
<p>Several neo-Nazi groups were active in Iran, although they are now defunct. Advocates of Nazism continue to exist in Iran and are mainly based on the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Nazism_in_Brazil" title="Nazism in Brazil">Nazism in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Several Brazilian neo-Nazi gangs appeared in the 1990s in <a href="/wiki/South_Region,_Brazil" title="South Region, Brazil">Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Southeast Region, Brazil">Southeastern Brazil</a>, regions with mostly white people, with their acts gaining more media coverage and public notoriety in the 2010s.<sup id="cite_ref-istoe_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-istoe-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spgaypride_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spgaypride-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nizkor_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nizkor-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Some members of Brazilian neo-Nazi groups have been associated with <a href="/wiki/Football_hooliganism" title="Football hooliganism">football hooliganism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Their targets have included African, South American and Asian immigrants; <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atheists" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheists">atheists</a>; <a href="/wiki/Afro-Brazilians" title="Afro-Brazilians">Afro-Brazilians</a> and internal migrants with origins in the northern regions of Brazil (who are mostly <a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">brown-skinned</a> or Afro-Brazilian);<sup id="cite_ref-nizkor_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nizkor-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Homelessness" title="Homelessness">homeless people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_Brazil" title="Prostitution in Brazil">prostitutes</a>;
