<a href="/wiki/Recreational_drug_use" title="Recreational drug use">recreational drug users</a>; <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminists</a> and—more frequently reported in the media—gay people, <a href="/wiki/Bisexuals" class="mw-redirect" title="Bisexuals">bisexuals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> and <a href="/wiki/Third_gender" title="Third gender">third-gender</a> people.<sup id="cite_ref-spgaypride_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spgaypride-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> News of their attacks has played a role in debates about <a href="/wiki/Anti-discrimination_laws_in_Brazil" title="Anti-discrimination laws in Brazil">anti-discrimination laws in Brazil</a> (including to some extent <a href="/wiki/Hate_speech" title="Hate speech">hate speech</a> laws) and the issues of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gender_identity" title="Gender identity">gender identity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism_in_Canada" title="Neo-Nazism in Canada">Neo-Nazism in Canada</a> began with the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Nazi_Party" title="Canadian Nazi Party">Canadian Nazi Party</a> in 1965. In the 1970s and 1980s, neo-Nazism continued to spread in the country as organizations including the <a href="/wiki/Western_Guard_Party" title="Western Guard Party">Western Guard Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Creativity_(religion)" title="Creativity (religion)">Church of the Creator</a> (later renamed <i>Creativity</i>) promoted white supremacist ideals.<sup id="cite_ref-source2_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source2-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Founded in the United States in 1973, Creativity calls for <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white people</a> to wage <a href="/wiki/Ben_Klassen#Racial_holy_war" title="Ben Klassen">racial holy war</a> (Rahowa) against Jews and other perceived enemies.<sup id="cite_ref-source14_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source14-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Don_Andrews" title="Don Andrews">Don Andrews</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Party_of_Canada" title="Nationalist Party of Canada">Nationalist Party of Canada</a> in 1977. The purported goals of the unregistered party are "the promotion and maintenance of European Heritage and Culture in Canada," but the party is known for anti-Semitism and racism. Many influential neo-Nazi Leaders, such as <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Droege" title="Wolfgang Droege">Wolfgang Droege</a>, were affiliated with the party, but many of its members left to join the Heritage Front, which was founded in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-source3_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source3-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Droege founded the <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Front" title="Heritage Front">Heritage Front</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> at a time when leaders of the white supremacist movement were "disgruntled about the state of the radical right" and wanted to unite unorganized groups of white supremacists into an influential and efficient group with common objectives.<sup id="cite_ref-source3_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source3-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>  Plans for the organization began in September 1989, and the formation of the Heritage Front was formally announced a couple of months later in November. In the 1990s, <a href="/wiki/George_Burdi" title="George Burdi">George Burdi</a> of <a href="/wiki/Resistance_Records" title="Resistance Records">Resistance Records</a> and the band <a href="/wiki/Rahowa_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rahowa (band)">Rahowa</a> popularized the Creativity movement and the <a href="/wiki/White_power_music" title="White power music">white power music</a> scene.<sup id="cite_ref-source1_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source1-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (October 2016)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Controversy and dissention has left many Canadian neo-Nazi organizations dissolved or weakened.<sup id="cite_ref-source3_162-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source3-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nazism_in_Chile" title="Nazism in Chile">Nazism in Chile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile.svg/170px-Flag_of_National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile.svg.png" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile.svg/255px-Flag_of_National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Flag_of_National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile.svg/340px-Flag_of_National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile" title="National Socialist Movement of Chile">National Socialist Movement of Chile</a></div></div></div>
<p>After the dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Movement_of_Chile" title="National Socialist Movement of Chile">National Socialist Movement of Chile</a> (MNSCH) in 1938, notable former members of MNSCH migrated into <a href="/wiki/Partido_Agrario_Laborista" class="mw-redirect" title="Partido Agrario Laborista">Partido Agrario Laborista</a> (PAL), obtaining high positions.<sup id="cite_ref-etche_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etche-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Not all former MNSCH members joined the PAL; some continued to form parties that followed the MNSCH model until 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-etche_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etche-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> A new old-school Nazi party was formed in 1964 by school teacher <a href="/wiki/Franz_Pfeiffer" title="Franz Pfeiffer">Franz Pfeiffer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-etche_164-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etche-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Among the activities of this group were the organization of a <i>Miss Nazi</i> beauty contest and the formation of a Chilean branch of the <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-etche_164-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etche-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The party disbanded in 1970. Pfeiffer attempted to restart it in 1983 in the wake of a wave of protests against the <a href="/wiki/Chile_under_Pinochet" class="mw-redirect" title="Chile under Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet regime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-etche_164-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etche-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Palacios" title="Nicolás Palacios">Nicolás Palacios</a> considered the "Chilean race" to be a mix of two bellicose master races: the <a href="/wiki/Visigoth" class="mw-redirect" title="Visigoth">Visigoths</a> of Spain and the <a href="/wiki/Mapuche" title="Mapuche">Mapuche</a> (Araucanians) of Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-palaciosmestizo_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palaciosmestizo-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>  Palacios traces the origins of the Spanish component of the "Chilean race" to the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, specifically to <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6taland" title="Götaland">Götaland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-palaciosmestizo_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palaciosmestizo-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> one of the supposed <a href="/wiki/Homeland" title="Homeland">homelands</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>. Palacios claimed that both the blonde-haired and the bronze-coloured Chilean <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizo</a> share a "moral physonomy" and a masculine psychology.<sup id="cite_ref-palaciospsico_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palaciospsico-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> He opposed immigration from <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a>, and argued that Mestizos who are derived from south Europeans lack "cerebral control" and are a social burden.<sup id="cite_ref-palacioslatino_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palacioslatino-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Costa_Rica">Costa Rica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Costa Rica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Several neo-Nazi groups exist in <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>. The first to receive attention was the <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rican_National_Socialist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Costa Rican National Socialist Party">Costa Rican National Socialist Party</a>, which is now disbanded.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Others include Costa Rican National Socialist Youth, Costa Rican National Socialist Alliance, New Social Order, Costa Rican National Socialist Resistance (which is Costa Rica's member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Union_of_National_Socialists" title="World Union of National Socialists">World Union of National Socialists</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> and the Hiperborean Spear Society. The groups normally target <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a>-<a href="/wiki/Costa_Ricans" title="Costa Ricans">Costa Ricans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afro-Costa_Rican" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Costa Rican">Afro-Costa Ricans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communists</a>, gay people and especially <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaraguan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colombian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian people">Colombian</a> immigrants. The media has discovered the existence of an underground neo-Nazi group inside the police.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Socialist_Movement_Rally_US_Capitol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/National_Socialist_Movement_Rally_US_Capitol.jpg/220px-National_Socialist_Movement_Rally_US_Capitol.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/National_Socialist_Movement_Rally_US_Capitol.jpg/330px-National_Socialist_Movement_Rally_US_Capitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/National_Socialist_Movement_Rally_US_Capitol.jpg/440px-National_Socialist_Movement_Rally_US_Capitol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3461" data-file-height="2203" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:National_Socialist_Movement_Rally_US_Capitol.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The NSM rally on the West lawn of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">US Capitol</a>, Washington DC, 2008</div></div></div>
<p>There are several neo-Nazi groups in the United States. The <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Movement_(United_States)" title="National Socialist Movement (United States)">National Socialist Movement</a> (NSM), with about 400 members in 32 states,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> is currently the largest neo-Nazi organization in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>  After World War II, new organizations formed with varying degrees of support for Nazi principles. The <a href="/wiki/National_States%27_Rights_Party" title="National States&#39; Rights Party">National States' Rights Party</a>, founded in 1958 by Edward Reed Fields and <a href="/wiki/J._B._Stoner" title="J. B. Stoner">J. B. Stoner</a> countered <a href="/wiki/Racial_integration" title="Racial integration">racial integration</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern United States</a> with Nazi-inspired publications and iconography. The <a href="/wiki/American_Nazi_Party" title="American Nazi Party">American Nazi Party</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/George_Lincoln_Rockwell" title="George Lincoln Rockwell">George Lincoln Rockwell</a> in 1959, achieved high-profile coverage in the press through its public demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First Amendment to the United States Constitution</a> guarantees <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>, which allows political organizations great latitude in expressing Nazi, racist, and anti-Semitic views. A First Amendment landmark case was <i><a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Party_of_America_v._Village_of_Skokie" title="National Socialist Party of America v. Village of Skokie">National Socialist Party of America v. Village of Skokie</a></i>, in which neo-Nazis threatened to march in a predominantly Jewish suburb of Chicago. The march never took place in Skokie, but the court ruling allowed the neo-Nazis to stage a series of demonstrations in Chicago.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Historical_Review" title="Institute for Historical Review">Institute for Historical Review</a>, formed in 1978, is a <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_denial" title="Holocaust denial">Holocaust denial</a> body associated with neo-Nazism.<sup id="cite_ref-ADL_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADL-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Organizations which report upon American neo-Nazi activities include the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Poverty_Law_Center" title="Southern Poverty Law Center">Southern Poverty Law Center</a>. American neo-Nazis are known to attack and harass minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (October 2016)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several groups in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Afrikaner_Weerstandsbeweging" title="Afrikaner Weerstandsbeweging">Afrikaner Weerstandsbeweging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blanke_Bevrydingsbeweging" title="Blanke Bevrydingsbeweging">Blanke Bevrydingsbeweging</a>, have often been described as neo-Nazi.<sup id="cite_ref-afrikaner_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrikaner-176">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_Terre%27Blanche" title="Eugène Terre&#39;Blanche">Eugène Terre'Blanche</a> was a prominent South African neo-Nazi leader who was murdered in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There were a number of now-defunct Australian neo-Nazi groups, such as the <a href="/wiki/Australian_National_Socialist_Party" title="Australian National Socialist Party">Australian National Socialist Party</a> (ANSP), which was formed in 1962 and merged into the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Party_of_Australia" title="National Socialist Party of Australia">National Socialist Party of Australia</a> (1968-1970s), originally a splinter group, in 1968,<sup id="cite_ref-Henderson_76_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson_76-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jack_van_Tongeren" title="Jack van Tongeren">Jack van Tongeren</a>'s Australian Nationalist Movement.<sup id="cite_ref-Henderson_76_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson_76-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Current active organisations include <a href="/wiki/Antipodean_Resistance" title="Antipodean Resistance">Antipodean Resistance</a>, local chapters of the Aryan Nations,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and Blood and Honour,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> as well as prominent individuals such as <a href="/wiki/Blair_Cottrell" class="mw-redirect" title="Blair Cottrell">Blair Cottrell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, historical neo-Nazi organisations include <a href="/wiki/Unit_88" title="Unit 88">Unit 88</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Party_of_New_Zealand" title="National Socialist Party of New Zealand">National Socialist Party of New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Current active organisations include the local chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Hammerskins" title="Hammerskins">Hammerskins</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> while White Nationalist organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_National_Front" title="New Zealand National Front">New Zealand National Front</a> have faced accusations of neo-Nazism.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neo-Nazism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Informational notes</b>
</p>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some of the fascistic old-guard from the pre-war ultra-nationalist movements were more skeptical of the benefits of the Rockwell-Jordan uniform scene. <a href="/wiki/Oswald_Mosley" title="Oswald Mosley">Oswald Mosley</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Union_Movement" title="Union Movement">Union Movement</a> described Jordan as, "a midget trying to walk in the boots of giants." Meanwhile, Yockeyism leaned more to the left than the "official" fascistic Pan-Europeanism of those which would become the <a href="/wiki/European_Social_Movement" title="European Social Movement">European Social Movement</a>. The latter associated with Mosley, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bard%C3%A8che" title="Maurice Bardèche">Maurice Bardèche</a> and others upheld a strictly "neither East, nor West", third position in regards to Soviet and American power.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">While the intelligence claims in regards to the Rockwell's American costume group proved unfounded, a number of actual German National Socialists did relocate to the Middle East, some conveted to Islam and changed their names; particularly Egypt and Syria. This includes <a href="/wiki/Johann_von_Leers" title="Johann von Leers">Johann von Leers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alois_Brunner" title="Alois Brunner">Alois Brunner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aribert_Heim" title="Aribert Heim">Aribert Heim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Stangl" title="Franz Stangl">Franz Stangl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Mertins" title="Gerhard Mertins">Gerhard Mertins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Eisele_(physician)" title="Hans Eisele (physician)">Hans Eisele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Rauff" title="Walter Rauff">Walter Rauff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artur_Schmitt" title="Artur Schmitt">Artur Schmitt</a> and others. The father of Neo-Nazism, Otto Ernst Remer, also fled to Egypt, then Syria during the 1950s.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

</p>

<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Gay, Kathlyn (1997) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=NWYLkF5NHVsC&amp;q=%22Neo-nazis%22+goals&amp;dq=%22Neo-nazis%22+goals&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwi3pYzk05raAhXjT98KHehxDawQ6AEINTAC"><i>Neo-Nazis: A Growing Threat</i></a>. Enslow. p.114. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780894909016" title="Special:BookSources/9780894909016">9780894909016</a>. <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">

It is a radically right-wing ideology, whose main characteristics are extreme nationalism and violent xenophobia. Neo-Nazism is, as the word suggests, a modern version of Nazism. In general, it is an incoherent right-extremist ideology, which is characterised by 'borrowing' many of the elements that constituted traditional Nazism.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Neo-Nazism&amp;rft.pub=The+Danish+Center+for+Holocaust+and+Genocide+Studies&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.au=Peter+Vogelsang&amp;rft.au=Brian+B.+M.+Larsen&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.holocaust-education.dk%2Feftertid%2Fnynazisme.asp&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANeo-Nazism" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></li>
